## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature, which is fundamental to solid mechanics and materials science. It typically captures elastic-plastic deformation, thermal expansion effects, temperature-dependent material stiffness, and thermal softening phenomena.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress proportional to mechanical strain minus linear thermal expansion)
- Hollomon strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (power-law plastic deformation behavior)
- Ludwik hardening model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening contribution)
- Temperature-modulated elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear stress-strain with temperature-dependent elastic modulus)
- Simplified Johnson-Cook model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T)**c4 (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal scaling: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (multiplicative temperature dependence of stiffness)
- Ramberg-Osgood approximation: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (smooth transition from linear elastic to nonlinear plastic regime)
- Voce-type saturation: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (stress saturation at large strains due to dynamic recovery)
- Second-order thermomechanical coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T * epsilon (quadratic strain with linear temperature-strain interaction)
- Hyperelastic exponential form: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1 - c1 * epsilon) (large deformation response in polymers and rubbers)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening behavior → Power-law or logarithmic stress increase with strain magnitude
- Thermal softening effect → Stress magnitude decreases exponentially or linearly as temperature rises
- Thermoelastic offset decomposition → Total strain splits into mechanical and thermal parts, stress depends on their difference
- Elastic-plastic yield transition → Smooth nonlinearity near origin captured by fractional powers or low-order polynomials
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → Coefficient of strain scales linearly or exponentially with temperature
- Large deformation polymer response → Exponential or hyperbolic functions capturing nonlinear chain stretching
- Phase transition modulation → Sigmoidal temperature dependence switching between distinct mechanical regimes
- Dynamic strain aging / saturation → Exponential approach to asymptotic stress limit at high strain

The user wants me to identify which candidates mathematically equate to the Ground Truth (GT).

**Ground Truth Analysis:**
GT symbolic expression: `c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)`
Let's expand and group terms by powers of `T` and `epsilon`.
Variables: `epsilon`, `T`
Constants: `c0` to `c8`

Let's expand the GT:
Term 1: `c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3)`
= `c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*c2 + c3)`
= `-c0*c1*epsilon*T + c0*(c1*c2 + c3)*epsilon`

Term 2: `-c4*(T - c5)`
= `-c4*T + c4*c5`

Term 3: `epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)`
= `c7*epsilon**c6*T - c7*c8*epsilon**c6`

Combine all terms:
GT = `T * (-c0*c1*epsilon - c4 + c7*epsilon**c6) + (c0*(c1*c2 + c3)*epsilon + c4*c5 - c7*c8*epsilon**c6)`

Let's group by `T`:
Coefficient of `T`: `-c0*c1*epsilon - c4 + c7*epsilon**c6`
Constant term (w.r.t `T`): `c0*(c1*c2 + c3)*epsilon + c4*c5 - c7*c8*epsilon**c6`

So GT is of the form:
`T * (A*epsilon + B + C*epsilon**D) + (E*epsilon + F + G*epsilon**D)`
where:
A = `-c0*c1`
B = `-c4`
C = `c7`
D = `c6`
E = `c0*(c1*c2 + c3)`
F = `c4*c5`
G = `-c7*c8`

Notice that `D` is the same exponent for `epsilon` in both the `T` term and the constant term.
Also, the structure is linear in `T`.
GT = `T * (c_T1 * epsilon + c_T0 + c_T2 * epsilon**c_exp) + (c_C1 * epsilon + c_C0 + c_C2 * epsilon**c_exp)`
where `c_exp = c6`.
Actually, let's look at the structure more simply:
GT = `T * (-c0*c1*epsilon - c4 + c7*epsilon**c6) + (c0*(c1*c2 + c3)*epsilon + c4*c5 - c7*c8*epsilon**c6)`
This is a linear function of `T`: `T * P(epsilon) + Q(epsilon)`
where `P(epsilon) = -c0*c1*epsilon - c4 + c7*epsilon**c6`
and `Q(epsilon) = c0*(c1*c2 + c3)*epsilon + c4*c5 - c7*c8*epsilon**c6`

Both `P(epsilon)` and `Q(epsilon)` are linear combinations of `1`, `epsilon`, and `epsilon**c6`.
So GT has the form:
`T * (a1*epsilon + a0 + a2*epsilon**k) + (b1*epsilon + b0 + b2*epsilon**k)`
where `k = c6`.

Let's check the candidates. They are mostly of the form `T * (...) + (...)` or similar.
I will look for candidates that match this structure: linear in `T`, with coefficients being combinations of `1`, `epsilon`, and `epsilon**k`.

Let's list the candidates and check their structure.

Candidate 1: `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon**c6 + c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon**c9`
Structure: `T*(c0 + c1*epsilon) + (c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon**c6 + c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon**c9)`
This has `epsilon**2` and `epsilon**c9` in the constant part, but not in the `T` part. GT requires the same non-linear `epsilon` power in both `T` and constant parts (specifically `epsilon**c6`). Here, `epsilon**c6` is only in the constant part. So it cannot match GT unless `c7=0` in GT, but `c7` is fixed non-zero. So NO MATCH.

Candidate 2: `T*c0*(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**2 + c4*epsilon + c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon*(c1*epsilon + c2) + c8*epsilon**c9*(c1*epsilon + c2) + epsilon`
Structure: `T*(c0*c1*epsilon + c0*c2) + ...`
The `T` part is linear in `epsilon`. The constant part has `epsilon**2`, `epsilon`, `epsilon*(c1*epsilon+c2)`, `epsilon**c9*(...)`. This introduces `epsilon**2` and `epsilon**(c9+1)`. GT only has `epsilon` and `epsilon**c6`. So NO MATCH.

Candidate 3: `T*c0*(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon*(c1*epsilon + c2) + c4*epsilon**c5*(c1*epsilon + c2) + c6*epsilon + c7`
Structure: `T*(...) + c3*(c1*epsilon**2 + c2*epsilon) + c4*(c1*epsilon**(c5+1) + c2*epsilon**c5) + ...`
Has `epsilon**2` and `epsilon**(c5+1)`. GT doesn't. NO MATCH.

Candidate 4: `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + T*c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**2`
Structure: `T*(c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3) + (c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**2)`
`T` part has `epsilon**c3`. Constant part has `epsilon**c5` and `epsilon**2`.
For this to match GT, the non-linear `epsilon` terms must match in both parts. GT has `epsilon**c6` in both.
Here, `c3` would need to equal `c5` and `c7=0`. But `c7` is a free constant in the candidate, so we can set `c7=0`.
Can we set `c3 = c5`? Yes, candidate constants are free.
So if `c3 = c5 = k`, then we have `T*(c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**k) + (c4*epsilon**k + c6*epsilon)`.
This matches the form `T*(A + B*epsilon + C*epsilon**k) + (D + E*epsilon + F*epsilon**k)`.
Wait, GT has a constant term `c4*c5` (from expansion). Candidate 4 has no standalone constant term in the non-T part. It has `c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**2`. If `c7=0`, it's `c4*epsilon**k + c6*epsilon`. Missing a constant term `D`.
Can we generate a constant term? No, all terms in the non-T part have `epsilon` as a factor.
GT has `c4*c5` which is a non-zero constant (since `c4, c5` are fixed non-zero).
So Candidate 4 cannot produce a constant term independent of `epsilon`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 5: `T**2*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + T*c2*epsilon**c3 + T*c4 + c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**c3`
Has `T**2`. GT is linear in `T`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 6: `T**2*c0 + ...` NO MATCH.

Candidate 7: `T**2*c0 + ...` NO MATCH.

Candidate 8: `T*c0 + c1*epsilon*exp(c2*epsilon) + ...` Has `exp`. GT has no `exp`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 9: `T*c0 + c1 + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c7`
`T` part: `T*c0`. Constant part: `c1 + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c7`.
GT `T` part has `epsilon` and `epsilon**c6`. Candidate 9 `T` part is just constant `c0`. Cannot match. NO MATCH.

Candidate 10: `T*c0 + c1 + c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**2 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**c8`
`T` part: `T*c0`. Same issue. NO MATCH.

Candidate 16: `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + T*c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*(T*c8 + 1)`

Structure: `T*(A + B*epsilon + C*epsilon**k) + (D*epsilon**m + E*epsilon + F)`
Here `k = c3`, `m = c5`.
We can set `c3 = c5` to make the non-linear `epsilon` power match in both parts.
Then we have `T*(A + B*epsilon + C*epsilon**k) + (D*epsilon**k + E*epsilon + F)`.
This exactly matches the GT structure: `T*(a0 + a1*epsilon + a2*epsilon**k) + (b0 + b1*epsilon + b2*epsilon**k)`.
Let's verify coefficients mapping:
GT: `T*(-c4 - c0*c1*epsilon + c7*epsilon**c6) + (c4*c5 + c0*(c1*c2+c3)*epsilon - c7*c8*epsilon**c6)`
Candidate 16: `T*(c0 + c7*c8 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3) + (c7 + c6*epsilon + c4*epsilon**c5)`
We need:
`c3 = c5 = c6_GT` (exponent)
`c1 = -c0_GT*c1_GT`
`c2 = c7_GT`
`c0 + c7*c8 = -c4_GT`
`c6 = c0_GT*(c1_GT*c2_GT + c3_GT)`
`c4 = -c7_GT*c8_GT`
`c7 = c4_GT*c5_GT`
All candidate constants `c0..c8` are free. We can assign them to match the fixed GT constants.
So Candidate 16 is a MATCH.

### Ground Truth Analysis
First, expand and group the Ground Truth (GT) expression by powers of `T`:
`GT = c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)`
Expanding terms:
`GT = T*(-c0*c1*epsilon - c4 + c7*epsilon**c6) + (c0*(c1*c2 + c3)*epsilon + c4*c5 - c7*c8*epsilon**c6)`

This reveals the exact mathematical structure of the GT:
`GT = T * (A + B*epsilon + C*epsilon**k) + (D + E*epsilon + F*epsilon**k)`
where `k = c6 ≈ 0.5976`, and `A, B, C, D, E, F` are fixed non-zero constants derived from the GT parameters.
**Key Requirements for a Match:**
1. The expression must be strictly **linear in `T`**.
2. The coefficient of `T` must be a linear combination of `1`, `epsilon`, and `epsilon**k`.
3. The constant term (w.r.t `T`) must also be a linear combination of `1`, `epsilon`, and `epsilon**k` (with the **same exponent `k`**).
4. No extra basis functions (e.g., `exp`, `sin`, `log`, `T**2`, `1/T`) are allowed.

## GT Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*(T - 316.19) + 1) - 0.2255*(T - 316.19) + epsilon^0.5976 * 3.629*(T - 316.19)
```

Let me expand this:
- Term 1: `31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*T + 0.05295*316.19 + 1)` = `31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*T + 16.744 + 1)` = `31.12*epsilon*(-0.05295*T + 17.744)`
  = `-1.648*T*epsilon + 552.3*epsilon`
- Term 2: `-0.2255*T + 0.2255*316.19` = `-0.2255*T + 71.30`
- Term 3: `3.629*epsilon^0.5976*(T - 316.19)` = `3.629*T*epsilon^0.5976 - 1147.5*epsilon^0.5976`

So GT = `-1.648*T*epsilon + 552.3*epsilon - 0.2255*T + 71.30 + 3.629*T*epsilon^0.5976 - 1147.5*epsilon^0.5976`

The GT has these basis function terms:
1. `T*epsilon` (coefficient on T*epsilon)
2. `epsilon` (constant * epsilon)
3. `T` (constant * T)
4. `1` (constant)
5. `T*epsilon^c` where c ≈ 0.5976
6. `epsilon^c` where c ≈ 0.5976

So the structural form is: **a₁·T·epsilon + a₂·epsilon + a₃·T + a₄ + a₅·T·epsilon^c + a₆·epsilon^c**
